   407	func TestExecuteShouldNotifyBeforeSpecEvent(t *testing.T) {
   408	        errs := gauge.NewBuildErrors()
   409	        r := &mockRunner{}
   410	        h := &mockPluginHandler{NotifyPluginsfunc: func(m *gauge_messages.Message) {}, GracefullyKillPluginsfunc: func() {}}
   411	
   412	        eventRaised := false
   413	        r.ExecuteAndGetStatusFunc = func(m *gauge_messages.Message) *gauge_messages.ProtoExecutionResult {
   414	                return &gauge_messages.ProtoExecutionResult{}
   415	        }
   416	
   417	        ch := make(chan event.ExecutionEvent)
   418	        event.InitRegistry()
   419	        event.Register(ch, event.SpecStart)
   420	        wg := &sync.WaitGroup{}
   421	        wg.Add(1)
   422	        go func() {
   423	                for {
   424	                        e := <-ch
   425	                        t.Log(e.Topic)
   426	                        if e.Topic == event.SpecStart {
   427	                                eventRaised = true
   428	                                wg.Done()
   429	                        }
   430	                }
   431	        }()
   432	        se := newSpecExecutor(exampleSpecWithScenarios, r, h, errs, 0)
   433	        se.execute(true, false, false)
   434	
   435	        wg.Wait()
   436	        if !eventRaised {
   437	                t.Error("Expected SpecStart event to be raised")
   438	        }
   439	        event.InitRegistry()
   440	}

   499	        if gotPostHookMessages[0] != "After Spec Called" {

2026-05-29 20:00:52,252 - INFO - swea-agent-getgauge__gauge-2836 - ========================= STEP 18 =========================
2026-05-29 20:00:52,256 - DEBUG - swea-lm-getgauge__gauge-2836 - n_cache_control: 2
2026-05-29 20:01:19,130 - DEBUG - swea-lm-getgauge__gauge-2836 - Response: ModelResponse(id='1449a2f6d4ef47539473853c0e073f3a', created=1780084853, model='DeepSeek-V4-Pro', object='chat.completion', system_fingerprint=None, choices=[Choices(finish_reason='tool_calls', index=0, message=Message(content='Now let me look more closely at the issue. I think the problem is in `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata`. When a scenario is retried:\n1. First attempt fails → `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata` adds the scenario to failedItemsMap\n2. Second attempt passes → `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata` does NOT add it (because `GetFailed()` returns false)\n\nBut the scenario is still in the failedItemsMap from the first attempt! The problem is that when a scenario passes on retry, we need to remove it from the failedItemsMap.\n\nBut actually, looking at `addSpecFailedMetadata`:\n```go\nfunc addSpecFailedMetadata(res result.Result, args []string) {\n    fileName := util.RelPathToProjectRoot(res.(*result.SpecResult).ProtoSpec.GetFileName())\n    delete(failedMeta.failedItemsMap, fileName)\n    failedMeta.addFailedItem(fileName, fileName)\n}\n```\n\nThis function is called on `SpecEnd` but only if the spec has pre/post hook failures. So if a spec has no hook failures, `addSpecFailedMetadata` is never called, and the failed scenarios from retries remain.\n\nBut wait, there\'s another issue. Even if `addSpecFailedMetadata` is called, it deletes ALL scenario-level entries for that spec and adds the spec-level filename. So if a spec has some failed scenarios and some that passed on retry, `addSpecFailedMetadata` would replace all of them with the spec-level filename. This would cause all scenarios in that spec to be re-run with `--failed`, not just the failed ones.\n\nLet me check the `addSuiteFailedMetadata` too:\n```go\nfunc addSuiteFailedMetadata(res result.Result, args []string) {\n    failedMeta.failedItemsMap = make(map[string]map[string]bool)\n    for _, arg := range args {\n        path, err := filepath.Abs(arg)\n        path = util.RelPathToProjectRoot(path)\n        if err == nil {\n            failedMeta.addFailedItem(path, path)\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis is called on `SuiteEnd` with pre/post hook failures. 2026-05-29 20:01:19,137 - INFO - swea-agent-getgauge__gauge-2836 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now let me look more closely at the issue. I think the problem is in `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata`. When a scenario is retried:
1. First attempt fails → `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata` adds the scenario to failedItemsMap
2. Second attempt passes → `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata` does NOT add it (because `GetFailed()` returns false)

But the scenario is still in the failedItemsMap from the first attempt! The problem is that when a scenario passes on retry, we need to remove it from the failedItemsMap.

But actually, looking at `addSpecFailedMetadata`:
```go
func addSpecFailedMetadata(res result.Result, args []string) {
    fileName := util.RelPathToProjectRoot(res.(*result.SpecResult).ProtoSpec.GetFileName())
    delete(failedMeta.failedItemsMap, fileName)
    failedMeta.addFailedItem(fileName, fileName)
}
```

This function is called on `SpecEnd` but only if the spec has pre/post hook failures. So if a spec has no hook failures, `addSpecFailedMetadata` is never called, and the failed scenarios from retries remain.

But wait, there's another issue. Even if `addSpecFailedMetadata` is called, it deletes ALL scenario-level entries for that spec and adds the spec-level filename. So if a spec has some failed scenarios and some that passed on retry, `addSpecFailedMetadata` would replace all of them with the spec-level filename. This would cause all scenarios in that spec to be re-run with `--failed`, not just the failed ones.

Let me check the `addSuiteFailedMetadata` too:
```go
func addSuiteFailedMetadata(res result.Result, args []string) {
    failedMeta.failedItemsMap = make(map[string]map[string]bool)
    for _, arg := range args {
        path, err := filepath.Abs(arg)
        path = util.RelPathToProjectRoot(path)
        if err == nil {
            failedMeta.addFailedItem(path, path)
        }
    }
}
```

This is called on `SuiteEnd` with pre/post hook failures. It clears the entire map and repopulates with args (spec dirs).

Now, the key question: How does `--failed` use this data?

Looking at `GetLastFailedState`:
```go
var GetLastFailedState = func() ([]string, error) {
    meta := readLastFailedState()
    util.SetWorkingDir(config.ProjectRoot)
    if len(meta.FailedItems) == 0 {
        return nil, errors.New("No failed tests found.")
    }
    return meta.args(), nil
}
```

And `args()`:
```go
func (m *failedMetadata) args() []string {
    return append(m.Args, m.FailedItems...)
}
```

So `--failed` reads `failures.json` and uses the `FailedItems` and `Args` to determine which specs/scenarios to run.

Now I think I understand the core issue: When a scenario fails on the first attempt but passes on retry, it's still added to `failedItemsMap` in `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata`. There's no mechanism to remove it when it passes on a subsequent retry.

The fix should be: When a scenario passes (either initially or on retry), we should remove it from the failed items map. Let me look at `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata` again:

```go
func prepareScenarioFailedMetadata(res *result.ScenarioResult, sce *gauge.Scenario, executionInfo *gauge_messages.ExecutionInfo) {
    if res.GetFailed() {
        specPath := executionInfo.GetCurrentSpec().GetFileName()
        failedScenario := util.RelPathToProjectRoot(specPath)
        failedMeta.addFailedItem(specPath, fmt.Sprintf("%s:%v", failedScenario, sce.Span.Start))
    }
}
```

The fix should be: when the scenario result is NOT failed, we should remove the item from the failedItemsMap. But actually, just removing it might not be enough because the scenario might not have been added in the first place (if it passed on the first attempt). We need to ensure that if a scenario passes, it's not in the failed items map.

Let me also check the `executeScenario` function again for the retry logic:

```go
func (e *specExecutor) executeScenario(scenario *gauge.Scenario) (*result.ScenarioResult, error) {
    ...
    for i := 0; i < MaxRetriesCount; i++ {
        ...
        scenarioResult = &result.ScenarioResult{...}
        ...
        e.scenarioExecutor.execute(scenario, scenarioResult)
        retriesCount++
        ...
        if !shouldRetry || !scenarioResult.GetFailed() {
            break
        }
    }
    scenarioResult.ProtoScenario.RetriesCount = int64(retriesCount)
    return scenarioResult, nil
}
```

So for each retry iteration, `scenarioExecutor.execute` is called, which fires `ScenarioStart` and `ScenarioEnd` events. If the first attempt fails, `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata` adds it. If the second attempt passes, `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata` does nothing (because `GetFailed()` is false), but the first attempt's failure remains.

The fix: In `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata`, when the result is NOT failed, we should remove the scenario from the failed items map. Let me also check if there's a case where a scenario could pass on the first attempt but we still want to keep it (no, we don't). So the fix is:

```go
func prepareScenarioFailedMetadata(res *result.ScenarioResult, sce *gauge.Scenario, executionInfo *gauge_messages.ExecutionInfo) {
    specPath := executionInfo.GetCurrentSpec().GetFileName()
    failedScenario := util.RelPathToProjectRoot(specPath)
    key := fmt.Sprintf("%s:%v", failedScenario, sce.Span.Start)
    if res.GetFailed() {
        failedMeta.addFailedItem(specPath, key)
    } else {
        // Remove from failed items if it passed (e.g., after retry)
        if _, ok := failedMeta.failedItemsMap[specPath]; ok {
            delete(failedMeta.failedItemsMap[specPath], key)
            if len(failedMeta.failedItemsMap[specPath]) == 0 {
                delete(failedMeta.failedItemsMap, specPath)
            }
        }
    }
}
```

Wait, but I should also consider the `addSpecFailedMetadata` and `addSuiteFailedMetadata` functions. Let me re-read them:

For `addSpecFailedMetadata`, it's called on `SpecEnd` when the spec has pre/post hook failures. It deletes the scenario-level entries and replaces with the spec-level filename. This seems correct because if a spec has hook failures, the whole spec failed.

For `addSuiteFailedMetadata`, it's called on `SuiteEnd` when the suite has pre/post hook failures. It clears everything and repopulates with the args (spec dirs). This also seems correct.

But the issue from the PR is about scenarios that pass after retry being included in `--failed`. So the fix should be in `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata`.

   147	        f.BoolVarP(&installPlugins, installPluginsName, "i", installPluginsDefault, "Install All Missing Plugins")
   148	        f.BoolVarP(&failed, failedName, "f", failedDefault, "Run only the scenarios failed in previous run. This cannot be used in conjunction with any other argument")
   149	        f.BoolVarP(&repeat, repeatName, "", repeatDefault, "Repeat last run. This cannot be used in conjunction with any other argument")
   150	        f.BoolVarP(&hideSuggestion, hideSuggestionName, "", hideSuggestionDefault, "Hide step implementation stub for every unimplemented step")
   151	        f.BoolVarP(&failSafe, failSafeName, "", failSafeDefault, "Force return 0 exit code, even in case of failures.")
   152	        f.BoolVarP(&skipCommandSave, skipCommandSaveName, "", skipCommandSaveDefault, "Skip saving last command in lastRunCmd.json")
   153	        err = f.MarkHidden(skipCommandSaveName)
   154	        if err != nil {
   155	                logger.Errorf(false, "Unable to mark '%s' flag as hidden: %s", skipCommandSaveName, err.Error())
   156	        }
   157	
   158	        f.StringArrayVar(&scenarios, scenarioName, scenarioNameDefault, "Set scenarios for running specs with scenario name")
   159	}
   160	
   161	func executeFailed(cmd *cobra.Command) {
   162	        lastState, err := rerun.GetLastFailedState()
   163	        if err != nil {
   164	                exit(err, "")
   165	        }
   166	        if !skipCommandSave {
   167	                rerun.WritePrevArgs(os.Args)
   168	        }
   169	        handleFlags(cmd, append([]string{"gauge"}, lastState...))
   170	        err = cmd.Flags().Set(skipCommandSaveName, "true")
   171	        if err != nil {
   172	                logger.Errorf(false, "Unable to set '%s' flag as 'true': %s", skipCommandSaveName, err.Error())
   173	        }
   174	        logger.Debugf(true, "Executing => %s\n", strings.Join(os.Args, " "))
   175	        err = cmd.Execute()
   176	        if err != nil {
   177	                logger.Errorf(true, "Unable to execute command %s: %s", cmd.Name(), err.Error())
   178	        }
   179	}
   180	
   181	func handleFlags(cmd *cobra.Command, args []string) {
   182	        cmd.Flags().Visit(func(flag *pflag.Flag) {
   183	                if !util.ListContains(overrideRerunFlags, flag.Name) && flag.Changed {
   184	                        err := flag.Value.Set(flag.DefValue)
   185	                        if err != nil {
   186	                                logger.Errorf(false, "Unable to set default value in '%s' flag: %s", flag.Name, err.Error())
   187	                        }
   188	                }
   189	        })
   190	
   191	        for i := 0; i <= len(args)-1; i++ {
   192	                f := lookupFlagFromArgs(cmd, args[i])
   193	                if f == nil {
   194	                        continue
   195	                }
   196	                v := f.Value.String()
   197	                _, err := strconv.ParseBool(v)
   198	                if err != nil && f.Changed {
   199	                        if strings.Contains(args[i], "=") {
   200	                                args[i] = strings.SplitAfter(args[i], "=")[0] + f.Value.String()
   201	                        } else {
   202	                                args[i+1] = v
   203	                                i = i + 1
   204	                        }
   205	                }
   206	        }
   207	        os.Args = args
   208	}
   209	
   210	func lookupFlagFromArgs(cmd *cobra.Command, arg string) *pflag.Flag {
   211	        fName := strings.Split(strings.TrimLeft(arg, "-"), "=")[0]
   212	        flags := cmd.Flags()
   213	        f := flags.Lookup(fName)
   214	        if f == nil && len(fName) == 1 {
   215	                f = flags.ShorthandLookup(fName)
   216	        }
   217	        return f
   218	}
   219	
   220	func addFlagsToExecutionArgs(flags *pflag.FlagSet) {
   221	        flags.Visit(func(flag *pflag.Flag) {
   222	                execution.ExecutionArgs = append(execution.ExecutionArgs, &gauge.ExecutionArg{
   223	                        Name:  flag.Name,
   224	                        Value: []string{flag.Value.String()},
   225	                })
   226	        })
   227	}
   228	
   229	func installMissingPlugins(flag, languageOnly bool) {
   230	        if flag && os.Getenv("GAUGE_PLUGIN_INSTALL") != "false" {
   231	                install.AllPlugins(machineReadable, languageOnly)
   232	        }
   233	}
   234	
   235	func execute(cmd *cobra.Command, args []string) {
   236	        for _, arg := range execution.ExecutionArgs {
   237	                logger.Debugf(true, "%s : %v", arg.Name, arg.Value)
   238	        }
   239	        loadEnvAndReinitLogger(cmd)
   240	        ensureScreenshotsDir()
   241	        if parallel && tagsToFilterForParallelRun != "" && !env.AllowFilteredParallelExecution() {
   242	                logger.Fatal(true, "Filtered parallel execution is a experimental feature. It can be enabled via allow_filtered_parallel_execution property.")
   243	        }
   244	        specs := getSpecsDir(args)
   245	        rerun.SaveState(os.Args[1:], specs)
   246	
   247	        // Save command args with auto-generated seed if needed
   248	        cmdArgsToSave := os.Args
   249	        if sort == "random" && randomSeed == 0 {
   250	                // Generate seed now so it can be saved for reruns
   251	                randomSeed = time.Now().UnixNano()
   252	                order.RandomSeed = randomSeed
   253	                // Append the seed to the command args for saving
   254	                cmdArgsToSave = append(os.Args, fmt.Sprintf("--%s=%d", randomSeedName, randomSeed))
   255	        }
   256	
   257	        if !skipCommandSave {
   258	                rerun.WritePrevArgs(cmdArgsToSave)
   259	        }
   260	        installMissingPlugins(installPlugins, false)
   261	        exitCode := execution.ExecuteSpecs(specs)
   262	        if failSafe && exitCode != execution.ParseFailed {
   263	                exitCode = 0
   264	        }
   265	        os.Exit(exitCode)
   266	}
   267	
   268	var repeatLastExecution = func(cmd *cobra.Command) {
   269	        lastState := rerun.ReadPrevArgs()
   270	        handleFlags(cmd, lastState)
   271	        logger.Debugf(true, "Executing => %s\n", strings.Join(lastState, " "))
   272	        err := cmd.Execute()
   273	        if err != nil {
   274	                logger.Errorf(true, "Unable to execute command %s: %s", cmd.Name(), err.Error())
   275	        }
   276	}
   277	
   278	func handleConflictingParams(setFlags *pflag.FlagSet, args []string) error {
   279	        flagDiffCount := 0
   280	        setFlags.Visit(func(flag *pflag.Flag) {
   281	                if !util.ListContains(overrideRerunFlags, flag.Name) && flag.DefValue != flag.Value.String() {
   282	                        flagDiffCount++
   283	                }
   284	        })
   285	        if repeat && len(args)+flagDiffCount > 1 {
   286	                return errors.New("Invalid Command. Usage: gauge run --repeat")
   287	        }
   288	        if failed && len(args)+flagDiffCount > 1 {
   289	                return errors.New("Invalid Command. Usage: gauge run --failed")
   290	        }
   291	        if !parallel && tagsToFilterForParallelRun != "" {
   292	                return errors.New("Invalid Command. flag --only can be used only with --parallel")
   293	        }
   294	        if maxRetriesCount == 1 && retryOnlyTags != "" {
   295	                return errors.New("Invalid Command. flag --retry-only can be used only with --max-retry-count")
   296	        }
   297	        return nil
   298	}
   299

package main

import (
    "fmt"
    "os"
    "path/filepath"
)

// Simulate the logic of prepareScenarioFailedMetadata
func main() {
    // The issue: when a scenario passes after retry, it should not be in the failed list
    // Let's trace through the code manually
    
    fmt.Println("=== Issue Analysis ===")

2026-05-29 20:02:31,348 - INFO - swea-agent-getgauge__gauge-2836 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I also need to consider the `addSpecFailedMetadata` function. Let me think about this more carefully.

The `addSpecFailedMetadata` is called on `SpecEnd` only when there are pre/post hook failures. When it's called, it deletes all scenario-level entries for that spec and replaces with the spec-level filename. This is fine because if a spec has hook failures, the whole spec is considered failed.

But there's another issue: if a spec has NO hook failures, `addSpecFailedMetadata` is never called, and the scenario-level failures from retries remain. My fix above addresses this.

However, I should also consider: what if a scenario fails on the first attempt, is added to the failed items map, but then passes on retry. The `addSpecFailedMetadata` (if called due to hook failures) would delete the scenario-level entries and add the spec-level entry. But if the spec doesn't have hook failures, `addSpecFailedMetadata` is not called, and my fix in `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata` handles the removal.

Now let me also check if there's an issue with the `addSpecFailedMetadata` function being called even when the spec passed overall (but had hook failures). Looking at the code:

```go
func addFailedMetadata(res result.Result, args []string, add func(res result.Result, args []string)) {
    if len(res.GetPostHook()) > 0 || len(res.GetPreHook()) > 0 {
        add(res, args)
    }
}
```

This is called on `SpecEnd` and `SuiteEnd`. If a spec has pre/post hook failures but the scenarios all passed (including after retries), the spec would be marked as failed in the failed items map. But actually, if there are hook failures, the spec IS considered failed regardless of scenario results, so this is correct.

But wait, there's another subtlety. The `addSpecFailedMetadata` function:
```go
func addSpecFailedMetadata(res result.Result, args []string) {
    fileName := util.RelPathToProjectRoot(res.(*result.SpecResult).ProtoSpec.GetFileName())
    delete(failedMeta.failedItemsMap, fileName)
    failedMeta.addFailedItem(fileName, fileName)
}
```

This deletes all scenario-level entries for that spec, even if some scenarios legitimately failed (not due to retry). It replaces them with the spec-level filename. So when `--failed` is run, the entire spec would be re-run, not just the failed scenarios. This might be intentional (since hook failures affect the whole spec), but it could also be a related issue.

However, the PR description specifically mentions scenarios that passed with --max-retry-count being executed again with --failed. So my fix addresses that by removing the scenario from failedItemsMap when it passes (even after retry).

Let me also check if there's a need to handle the case where `addSpecFailedMetadata` should only mark the spec as failed if it actually failed (not just because of hook failures that might have been resolved). But that's beyond the scope of this PR.

Let me now verify the test file to ensure my changes are consistent with the existing tests:

The existing test `TestGetScenarioFailedMetadata` tests that a failed scenario is added. My change doesn't break this test because the scenario result is FAILED, so it will still be added.\n\nNow let me think about edge cases:\n\n1. **Scenario passes on first attempt**: `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata` is called with `GetFailed() == false`. With my change, it tries to delete the key from `failedItemsMap[specPath]`. If the key doesn't exist (which it won't since it passed on first attempt), the delete is a no-op, and the check `if _, ok := failedMeta.failedItemsMap[specPath]` returns false (since the specPath key doesn't exist), so nothing happens. This is correct.\n\n2. **Scenario fails on first attempt, passes on second**: First call adds it, second call removes it. Correct.\n\n3. **Scenario fails on all attempts**: Each call adds it (same key, same map). The first call adds it, subsequent calls just set the same key to true again. It stays in the map. Correct.\n\n4. **Multiple scenarios in the same spec, one passes after retry and one fully fails**: The one that passes after retry gets removed, the one that fully fails stays. Correct.\n\n5. **Scenario fails, then passes, then spec has hook failures**: `addSpecFailedMetadata` will delete all scenario-level entries for that spec and add the spec-level filename. This is correct because hook failures mean the whole spec failed.\n\nBut wait, there's another edge case I need to think about:\n\n6. **What if `addSpecFailedMetadata` is called but the spec actually passed (scenarios all passed after retries)?** If the spec has hook failures, `addSpecFailedMetadata` marks the whole spec as failed. But hooks are run only once per spec, not per retry. If a hook fails, the spec is legitimately failed. So this is correct.\n\nBut actually, looking at the flow more carefully: `addFailedMetadata` is called on `SpecEnd` with `addSpecFailedMetadata`. The condition is:\n```go\nfunc addFailedMetadata(res result.Result, args []string, add func(res result.Result, args []string)) {\n    if len(res.GetPostHook()) > 0 || len(res.GetPreHook()) > 0 {\n        add(res, args)\n    }\n}\n```\n\nSo `addSpecFailedMetadata` is only called if the spec has pre/post hook failures. In `addSpecFailedMetadata`:\n```go\nfunc addSpecFailedMetadata(res result.Result, args []string) {\n    fileName := util.RelPathToProjectRoot(res.(*result.SpecResult).ProtoSpec.GetFileName())\n    delete(failedMeta.failedItemsMap, fileName)\n    failedMeta.addFailedItem(fileName, fileName)\n}\n```\n\nThis deletes all scenario-level entries and adds the spec-level filename. This means for a spec with hook failures, all scenarios (including those that passed after retry) will be re-run with `--failed`. But that's the intended behavior because hook failures are at the spec level, not scenario level.\n\nNow I also need to think about another edge case: what if a scenario is part of a data-driven spec/table-driven scenario? Looking at the code:\n\nIn `specExecutor.executeScenarioTableDrivenScenarios` (line 161-175), each table-driven scenario calls `executeScenario`, which fires events. So my fix should work for table-driven scenarios too.\n\nLet me also check if there's any other place that might need changes. Let me look at the `addSpecFailedMetadata` function more carefully. 2026-05-29 20:03:01,934 - INFO - swea-agent-getgauge__gauge-2836 - 💭 THOUGHT
Good. The existing test `TestGetScenarioFailedMetadata` tests that a failed scenario is added. My change doesn't break this test because the scenario result is FAILED, so it will still be added.

Now let me think about edge cases:

1. **Scenario passes on first attempt**: `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata` is called with `GetFailed() == false`. With my change, it tries to delete the key from `failedItemsMap[specPath]`. If the key doesn't exist (which it won't since it passed on first attempt), the delete is a no-op, and the check `if _, ok := failedMeta.failedItemsMap[specPath]` returns false (since the specPath key doesn't exist), so nothing happens. This is correct.

2. **Scenario fails on first attempt, passes on second**: First call adds it, second call removes it. Correct.

3. **Scenario fails on all attempts**: Each call adds it (same key, same map). The first call adds it, subsequent calls just set the same key to true again. It stays in the map. Correct.

4. **Multiple scenarios in the same spec, one passes after retry and one fully fails**: The one that passes after retry gets removed, the one that fully fails stays. Correct.

5. **Scenario fails, then passes, then spec has hook failures**: `addSpecFailedMetadata` will delete all scenario-level entries for that spec and add the spec-level filename. This is correct because hook failures mean the whole spec failed.

But wait, there's another edge case I need to think about:

6. **What if `addSpecFailedMetadata` is called but the spec actually passed (scenarios all passed after retries)?** If the spec has hook failures, `addSpecFailedMetadata` marks the whole spec as failed. But hooks are run only once per spec, not per retry. If a hook fails, the spec is legitimately failed. So this is correct.

But actually, looking at the flow more carefully: `addFailedMetadata` is called on `SpecEnd` with `addSpecFailedMetadata`. The condition is:
```go
func addFailedMetadata(res result.Result, args []string, add func(res result.Result, args []string)) {
    if len(res.GetPostHook()) > 0 || len(res.GetPreHook()) > 0 {
        add(res, args)
    }
}
```

So `addSpecFailedMetadata` is only called if the spec has pre/post hook failures. In `addSpecFailedMetadata`:
```go
func addSpecFailedMetadata(res result.Result, args []string) {
    fileName := util.RelPathToProjectRoot(res.(*result.SpecResult).ProtoSpec.GetFileName())
    delete(failedMeta.failedItemsMap, fileName)
    failedMeta.addFailedItem(fileName, fileName)
}
```

This deletes all scenario-level entries and adds the spec-level filename. This means for a spec with hook failures, all scenarios (including those that passed after retry) will be re-run with `--failed`. But that's the intended behavior because hook failures are at the spec level, not scenario level.

Now I also need to think about another edge case: what if a scenario is part of a data-driven spec/table-driven scenario? Looking at the code:

In `specExecutor.executeScenarioTableDrivenScenarios` (line 161-175), each table-driven scenario calls `executeScenario`, which fires events. So my fix should work for table-driven scenarios too.

Let me also check if there's any other place that might need changes. Let me look at the `addSpecFailedMetadata` function more carefully. Currently, it unconditionally deletes all scenario-level entries and adds the spec-level filename when there are hook failures. But what if some scenarios in the spec truly failed (not just retry-related)? They would be removed and replaced by the spec-level filename, meaning the whole spec would be re-run. This seems intentional.

But there's another case I should consider: `addSpecFailedMetadata` is also called when the spec has NO hook failures? No, it's only called when `len(res.GetPostHook()) > 0 || len(res.GetPreHook()) > 0`. So if a spec has no hook failures, `addSpecFailedMetadata` is never called, and only scenario-level failures are tracked. This is where my fix matters most.

    32	var failedMeta *failedMetadata

    34	func init() {
    35	        failedMeta = newFailedMetaData()
    36	}

    38	type failedMetadata struct {
    39	        Args           []string
    40	        failedItemsMap map[string]map[string]bool
    41	        FailedItems    []string
    42	}
    43	
    44	func (m *failedMetadata) args() []string {
    45	        return append(m.Args, m.FailedItems...)
    46	}
    47	
    48	func (m *failedMetadata) getFailedItems() []string {
    49	        failedItems := []string{}
    50	        for _, v := range m.failedItemsMap {
    51	                for k := range v {
    52	                        failedItems = append(failedItems, k)
    53	                }
    54	        }
    55	        return failedItems
    56	}
    57	
    58	func (m *failedMetadata) aggregateFailedItems() {
    59	        m.FailedItems = m.getFailedItems()
    60	}
    61	
    62	func newFailedMetaData() *failedMetadata {
    63	        return &failedMetadata{Args: make([]string, 0), failedItemsMap: make(map[string]map[string]bool), FailedItems: []string{}}
    64	}
    65	
    66	func (m *failedMetadata) addFailedItem(itemName string, item string) {
    67	        if _, ok := m.failedItemsMap[itemName]; !ok {
    68	                m.failedItemsMap[itemName] = make(map[string]bool)
    69	        }
    70	        m.failedItemsMap[itemName][item] = true
    71	}
    72	
    73	// ListenFailedScenarios listens to execution events and writes the failed scenarios to JSON file
    74	func ListenFailedScenarios(wg *sync.WaitGroup, specDirs []string) {
    75	        ch := make(chan event.ExecutionEvent)
    76	        event.Register(ch, event.ScenarioEnd)
    77	        event.Register(ch, event.SpecEnd)
    78	        event.Register(ch, event.SuiteEnd)
    79	        wg.Add(1)
    80	
    81	        go func() {
    82	                for {
    83	                        e := <-ch
    84	                        switch e.Topic {
    85	                        case event.ScenarioEnd:
    86	                                prepareScenarioFailedMetadata(e.Result.(*result.ScenarioResult), e.Item.(*gauge.Scenario), e.ExecutionInfo)
    87	                        case event.SpecEnd:
    88	                                addFailedMetadata(e.Result, specDirs, addSpecFailedMetadata)
    89	                        case event.SuiteEnd:
    90	                                addFailedMetadata(e.Result, specDirs, addSuiteFailedMetadata)
    91	                                failedMeta.aggregateFailedItems()
    92	                                writeFailedMeta(getJSON(failedMeta))
    93	                                wg.Done()
    94	                        }
    95	                }
    96	        }()
    97	}
    98	
    99	func prepareScenarioFailedMetadata(res *result.ScenarioResult, sce *gauge.Scenario, executionInfo *gauge_messages.ExecutionInfo) {
   100	        specPath := executionInfo.GetCurrentSpec().GetFileName()
   101	        failedScenario := util.RelPathToProjectRoot(specPath)
   102	        key := fmt.Sprintf("%s:%v", failedScenario, sce.Span.Start)
   103	        if res.GetFailed() {
   104	                failedMeta.addFailedItem(specPath, key)
   105	        } else {
   106	                if _, ok := failedMeta.failedItemsMap[specPath]; ok {
   107	                        delete(failedMeta.failedItemsMap[specPath], key)
   108	                        if len(failedMeta.failedItemsMap[specPath]) == 0 {
   109	                                delete(failedMeta.failedItemsMap, specPath)
   110	                        }
   111	                }
   112	        }
   113	}
   114	
   115	func addSpecFailedMetadata(res result.Result, args []string) {
   116	        fileName := util.RelPathToProjectRoot(res.(*result.SpecResult).ProtoSpec.GetFileName())
   117	        delete(failedMeta.failedItemsMap, fileName)
   118	        failedMeta.addFailedItem(fileName, fileName)
   119	}
   120	
   121	func addSuiteFailedMetadata(res result.Result, args []string) {
   122	        failedMeta.failedItemsMap = make(map[string]map[string]bool)
   123	        for _, arg := range args {
   124	                path, err := filepath.Abs(arg)
   125	                path = util.RelPathToProjectRoot(path)
   126	                if err == nil {
   127	                        failedMeta.addFailedItem(path, path)
   128	                }
   129	        }
   130	}
   131	
   132	func addFailedMetadata(res result.Result, args []string, add func(res result.Result, args []string)) {
   133	        if len(res.GetPostHook()) > 0 || len(res.GetPreHook()) > 0 {
   134	                add(res, args)
   135	        }
   136	}
   137	
   138	func writeFailedMeta(contents string) {
   139	        failuresFile := filepath.Join(config.ProjectRoot, common.DotGauge, failedFile)
   140	        dotGaugeDir := filepath.Join(config.ProjectRoot, common.DotGauge)
   141	        if err := os.MkdirAll(dotGaugeDir, common.NewDirectoryPermissions); err != nil {
   142	                logger.Fatalf(true, "Failed to create directory in %s. Reason: %s", dotGaugeDir, err.Error())
   143	        }
   144	        err := os.WriteFile(failuresFile, []byte(contents), common.NewFilePermissions)
   145	        if err != nil {
   146	                logger.Fatalf(true, "Failed to write to %s. Reason: %s", failuresFile, err.Error())
   147	        }
   148	}
   149	
   150	func getJSON(failedMeta *failedMetadata) string {
   151	        j, err := json.MarshalIndent(failedMeta, "", "\t")
   152	        if err != nil {
   153	                logger.Warningf(true, "Failed to save run info. Reason: %s", err.Error())
   154	        }
   155	        return string(j)
   156	}
   157	
   158	var GetLastFailedState = func() ([]string, error) {
   159	        meta := readLastFailedState()
   160	        util.SetWorkingDir(config.ProjectRoot)
   161	        if len(meta.FailedItems) == 0 {
   162	                return nil, errors.New("No failed tests found.")
   163	        }
   164	        return meta.args(), nil
   165	}
   166	
   167	func SaveState(args []string, specs []string) {
   168	        isPresent := func(values []string, value string) bool {
   169	                for _, v := range values {
   170	                        if v == value {
   171	                                return true
   172	                        }
   173	                }
   174	                return false
   175	        }
   176	        for _, a := range args {
   177	                if !isPresent(specs, a) {
   178	                        failedMeta.Args = append(failedMeta.Args, a)
   179	                }
   180	        }
   181	}
   182	
   183	func readLastFailedState() *failedMetadata {
   184	        contents, err := common.ReadFileContents(filepath.Join(config.ProjectRoot, common.DotGauge, failedFile))
   185	        if err != nil {
   186	                logger.Fatalf(true, "Failed to read last run information. Reason: %s", err.Error())
   187	        }
   188	        meta := newFailedMetaData()
   189	        if err = json.Unmarshal([]byte(contents), meta); err != nil {
   190	                logger.Fatalf(true, "Invalid last run information. Reason: %s", err.Error())
   191	        }
   192	        return meta
   193	}
   194	
   195	var ReadPrevArgs = func() []string {
   196	        contents, err := common.ReadFileContents(filepath.Join(config.ProjectRoot, common.DotGauge, lastRunCmdFileName))
   197	        if err != nil {
   198	                logger.Fatalf(true, "Failed to read previous command information. Reason: %s", err.Error())
   199	                return nil
   200	        }
   201	        var args []string
   202	        if err = json.Unmarshal([]byte(contents), &args); err != nil {
   203	                logger.Fatalf(true, "Invalid previous command information. Reason: %s", err.Error())
   204	                return nil
   205	        }
   206	        return args
   207	}
   208	
   209	var WritePrevArgs = func(cmdArgs []string) {
   210	        b, err := json.MarshalIndent(cmdArgs, "", "\t")
   211	        if err != nil {

   218	        }

2026-05-29 20:03:54,276 - INFO - swea-agent-getgauge__gauge-2836 - 💭 THOUGHT
Let me now think about whether my change is sufficient. Let me re-analyze the problem:

The PR description says:
1. Perform an execution with `max-retry-count=2`
2. Some tests will pass after 1 retry
3. Perform `gauge run --failed`
4. Failed tests and those who passed with `max-retry-count=2` will execute

So the issue is that scenarios that passed after retry are still in the `failures.json` file and get re-executed with `--failed`.

My fix addresses this by removing the scenario from `failedItemsMap` when it passes (which happens on the retry that succeeds).

But wait, I need to also consider: what if the scenario fails on the last retry? In that case:
- All retries result in `GetFailed() == true`, so each call adds the scenario to failedItemsMap. It stays there. Correct.
- The scenario is ultimately failed, and `--failed` should re-run it. Correct.

What if the scenario passes on the first attempt (no retries needed)?
- `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata` is called once with `GetFailed() == false`. My code tries to delete it, but it was never added, so nothing happens. Correct.

What if the scenario passes on the second attempt (first attempt fails)?
- First call: `GetFailed() == true` → added to failedItemsMap
- Second call: `GetFailed() == false` → removed from failedItemsMap
- `--failed` will NOT re-run it. Correct.

What if the scenario passes on the third attempt (first two fail)?
- First call: `GetFailed() == true` → added
- Second call: `GetFailed() == true` → added (same key, no-op)
- Third call: `GetFailed() == false` → removed
- Correct.

Now, there's also another consideration: `addSpecFailedMetadata`. This is called on `SpecEnd` if the spec has pre/post hook failures. It deletes all scenario-level entries and adds the spec-level filename. If a spec has hook failures, it would override my fix and mark the entire spec as failed. But as I said, this is correct because hook failures are at the spec level.

However, there's a potential issue: `addSpecFailedMetadata` is only called if the spec has pre/post hook failures. If the spec has NO hook failures, `addSpecFailedMetadata` is never called, and only scenario-level entries are used. My fix ensures that scenarios that passed after retry are removed from the scenario-level entries.

But what about the case where ALL scenarios in a spec passed after retry, and the spec has no hook failures? Then `failedItemsMap` would be empty for that spec, and the spec would not be included in `--failed`. Correct.

What about the case where SOME scenarios passed after retry and SOME failed? The failed ones remain in `failedItemsMap`, and the passed-after-retry ones are removed. Correct.

Now, let me also think about whether `addSpecFailedMetadata` should also consider the retry status. Currently, it doesn't. It unconditionally marks the spec as failed if there are hook failures. But what if the hook failure was on a retry and then the hook passed on a subsequent retry? Well, hooks are not retried - they are run once per spec/scenario. So if a hook fails, the spec/scenario is failed, period.

Let me also check if there's any issue with the `addSuiteFailedMetadata` function. It's called on `SuiteEnd` with pre/post hook failures. It clears the entire `failedItemsMap` and repopulates with the args (spec dirs). This means if there's a suite-level hook failure, ALL specs in the args are considered failed. This seems correct for suite-level hook failures.

I think my fix is complete and correct.

But wait, I need to double-check one more thing. Let me look at the `executeScenario` function again:

```go
func (e *specExecutor) executeScenario(scenario *gauge.Scenario) (*result.ScenarioResult, error) {
    ...
    for i := 0; i < MaxRetriesCount; i++ {
        ...
        scenarioResult = &result.ScenarioResult{...}
        ...
        e.scenarioExecutor.execute(scenario, scenarioResult)
        retriesCount++
        ...
        if !shouldRetry || !scenarioResult.GetFailed() {
            break
        }
    }
    scenarioResult.ProtoScenario.RetriesCount = int64(retriesCount)
    return scenarioResult, nil
}
```

And `scenarioExecutor.execute`:
```go
func (e *scenarioExecutor) execute(i gauge.Item, r result.Result) {
    ...
    event.Notify(event.NewExecutionEvent(event.ScenarioStart, scenario, scenarioResult, e.stream, e.currentExecutionInfo))
    defer event.Notify(event.NewExecutionEvent(event.ScenarioEnd, scenario, scenarioResult, e.stream, e.currentExecutionInfo))
    ...
}
```

So for each retry iteration, `ScenarioStart` and `ScenarioEnd` events are fired. In the `ListenFailedScenarios` function, only `ScenarioEnd` is handled. So for each retry, `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata` is called with the current result.

On the first retry (which fails), the scenario is added to `failedItemsMap`.
On the second retry (which passes), my fix removes it.

But what about the initial state? On the first retry, if the scenario fails, it's added. On the second retry, if it passes, it's removed. But what if there are more than 2 retries and the scenario fails, fails, passes? First adds, second adds (no-op), third removes. Correct.

Now, is there any race condition? The events are handled in a single goroutine (the one in `ListenFailedScenarios`), so there shouldn't be any race condition.

I'm fairly confident that my fix is correct. But let me also think about whether there's another approach that might be cleaner: instead of removing the scenario on pass, we could clear the failedItemsMap for a scenario at the beginning of each retry, and only add it if the final result is failed. But that would require changes in `executeScenario` to signal the beginning of a retry, which is more complex.

My approach is simpler and correct: if a scenario passes (regardless of whether it's a retry or first attempt), it should not be in the failed items map. If it fails, it should be added. The only caveat is if a scenario passes on the first attempt, we try to delete a non-existent key, which is a no-op (safe because we check if the map exists first).

Let me also consider: what if `prepareScenarioFailedMetadata` is called for a scenario that was never added to `failedItemsMap` (e.g., a scenario that passed on the first attempt)? My code checks `if _, ok := failedMeta.failedItemsMap[specPath]; ok` before attempting to delete. If the specPath doesn't exist in `failedItemsMap`, the delete is skipped. This is safe.

What if the specPath exists in `failedItemsMap` but the specific key doesn't? `delete` on a non-existent key is a no-op in Go. So even if we skip the check, it would be safe. But we also need to check if the inner map becomes empty and delete the outer key. My code does that.

I think the fix is complete. Let me also check if there's a similar issue with `parallelExecution.go` or `parallelGrpcExecution.go` that might need changes:



🎬 ACTION

    33	// Strategy for execution, can be either 'Eager' or 'Lazy'
    34	var Strategy string
    35	
    36	// Eager is a parallelization strategy for execution. In this case tests are distributed before execution, thus making them an equal number based distribution.
    37	const Eager string = "eager"
    38	
    39	// Lazy is a parallelization strategy for execution. In this case tests assignment will be dynamic during execution, i.e. assign the next spec in line to the stream that has completed it’s previous execution and is waiting for more work.

    74	type streamExecError struct {
    75	        specsSkipped []string
    76	        message      string
    77	}
    78	
    79	func (s streamExecError) Error() string {
    80	        var specNames string
    81	        for _, spec := range s.specsSkipped {
    82	                specNames += fmt.Sprintf("%s\n", spec)
    83	        }
    84	        return fmt.Sprintf("The following specifications could not be executed:\n%sReason : %s.", specNames, s.message)
    85	}
    86	
    87	func (e *parallelExecution) numberOfStreams() int {
    88	        nStreams := e.numberOfExecutionStreams
    89	        size := e.specCollection.Size()
    90	        if nStreams > size {
    91	                nStreams = size
    92	        }
    93	        return nStreams
    94	}
    95	
    96	func (e *parallelExecution) start() {
    97	        e.startTime = time.Now()
    98	        event.Notify(event.NewExecutionEvent(event.SuiteStart, nil, nil, 0, &gauge_messages.ExecutionInfo{}))
    99	        e.pluginHandler = plugin.StartPlugins(e.manifest)
   100	}
   101	
   102	func (e *parallelExecution) startRunnersForRemainingStreams() {
   103	        totalStreams := e.numberOfStreams()
   104	        rChan := make(chan runner.Runner, totalStreams-1)
   105	        for i := 2; i <= totalStreams; i++ {
   106	                go func(stream int) {
   107	                        r, err := e.startRunner(e.specCollection, stream)
   108	                        if len(err) > 0 {
   109	                                e.resultChan <- &result.SuiteResult{UnhandledErrors: err}
   110	                                return
   111	                        }
   112	                        rChan <- r
   113	                }(i)
   114	        }
   115	        for i := 1; i < totalStreams; i++ {
   116	                e.runners = append(e.runners, <-rChan)
   117	        }
   118	}
   119	
   120	func (e *parallelExecution) run() *result.SuiteResult {
   121	        e.start()
   122	        var res []*result.SuiteResult
   123	        if env.AllowFilteredParallelExecution() && e.tagsToFilter != "" {
   124	                parallesSpecs, serialSpecs := filter.FilterSpecForParallelRun(e.specCollection.Specs(), e.tagsToFilter)
   125	                if Verbose {
   126	                        logger.Infof(true, "Applied tags '%s' to filter specs for parallel execution", e.tagsToFilter)
   127	                        logger.Infof(true, "No of specs to be executed in serial : %d", len(serialSpecs))
   128	                        logger.Infof(true, "No of specs to be executed in parallel : %d", len(parallesSpecs))
   129	                }
   130	                if len(serialSpecs) > 0 {
   131	                        logger.Infof(true, "Executing %d specs in serial.", len(serialSpecs))
   132	                        e.specCollection = gauge.NewSpecCollection(parallesSpecs, false)
   133	                        res = append(res, e.executeSpecsInSerial(gauge.NewSpecCollection(serialSpecs, true)))
   134	                }
   135	        }
   136	
   137	        if e.specCollection.Size() > 0 {
   138	                logger.Infof(true, "Executing in %d parallel streams.", e.numberOfStreams())
   139	                // skipcq CRT-A0013
   140	                if e.isMultithreaded() {
   141	                        logger.Debugf(true, "Using multithreading for parallel execution.")
   142	                        if e.runners[0].Info().GRPCSupport {
   143	                                go e.executeGrpcMultithreaded()
   144	                        } else {
   145	                                go e.executeLegacyMultithreaded()
   146	                        }
   147	                } else if isLazy() {
   148	                        go e.executeLazily()
   149	                } else {
   150	                        go e.executeEagerly()
   151	                }
   152	
   153	                for r := range e.resultChan {
   154	                        res = append(res, r)
   155	                }
   156	        } else {
   157	                logger.Infof(true, "No specs remains to execute in parallel.")
   158	        }
   159	        e.aggregateResults(res)
   160	        e.finish()
   161	        return e.suiteResult
   162	}
   163	
   164	func (e *parallelExecution) executeLazily() {
   165	        defer close(e.resultChan)
   166	        e.wg.Add(e.numberOfStreams())
   167	        e.startRunnersForRemainingStreams()
   168	
   169	        for i := 1; i <= len(e.runners); i++ {
   170	                go func(stream int) {
   171	                        defer e.wg.Done()
   172	                        e.startSpecsExecutionWithRunner(e.specCollection, e.runners[stream-1], stream)
   173	                }(i)
   174	        }
   175	        e.wg.Wait()
   176	}
   177	
   178	func (e *parallelExecution) executeLegacyMultithreaded() {
   179	        defer close(e.resultChan)
   180	        totalStreams := e.numberOfStreams()
   181	        e.wg.Add(totalStreams)
   182	        handlers := make([]*conn.GaugeConnectionHandler, 0)
   183	        var ports []string
   184	        for i := 0; i < totalStreams; i++ {
   185	                port, err := conn.GetPortFromEnvironmentVariable(common.GaugePortEnvName)
   186	                if err != nil {
   187	                        port = 0
   188	                }
   189	                handler, err := conn.NewGaugeConnectionHandler(port, nil)
   190	                if err != nil {
   191	                        logger.Errorf(true, "failed to create handler. %s", err.Error())
   192	                }
   193	                ports = append(ports, strconv.Itoa(handler.ConnectionPortNumber()))
   194	                handlers = append(handlers, handler)
   195	        }
   196	        _ = os.Setenv(gaugeAPIPortsEnv, strings.Join(ports, ","))
   197	        writer := logger.NewLogWriter(e.manifest.Language, true, 0)
   198	        r, err := runner.StartLegacyRunner(e.manifest, "0", writer, make(chan bool), false)
   199	        if err != nil {
   200	                logger.Fatalf(true, "failed to start runner. %s", err.Error())
   201	        }
   202	        for i := 0; i < totalStreams; i++ {
   203	                connection, err := handlers[i].AcceptConnection(config.RunnerConnectionTimeout(), make(chan error))
   204	                if err != nil {
   205	                        logger.Error(true, err.Error())
   206	                }
   207	                crapRunner := &runner.MultithreadedRunner{}
   208	                crapRunner.SetConnection(connection)
   209	                go e.startMultithreaded(crapRunner, e.resultChan, i+1)
   210	        }
   211	        e.wg.Wait()
   212	        err = r.Cmd.Process.Kill()
   213	        if err != nil {
   214	                logger.Infof(true, "unable to kill runner: %s", err.Error())
   215	        }
   216	}
   217	
   218	func (e *parallelExecution) startMultithreaded(r runner.Runner, resChan chan *result.SuiteResult, stream int) {
   219	        defer e.wg.Done()
   220	        e.startSpecsExecutionWithRunner(e.specCollection, r, stream)
   221	}
   222	
   223	func (e *parallelExecution) executeEagerly() {
   224	        defer close(e.resultChan)
   225	        distributions := e.numberOfStreams()
   226	        specs := filter.DistributeSpecs(e.specCollection.Specs(), distributions)
   227	        e.wg.Add(distributions)
   228	        e.startRunnersForRemainingStreams()
   229	
   230	        for i, s := range specs {
   231	                i, s := i, s
   232	                go func(j int) {
   233	                        defer e.wg.Done()
   234	                        e.startSpecsExecutionWithRunner(s, e.runners[j], j+1)
   235	                }(i)
   236	        }
   237	        e.wg.Wait()
   238	}
   239	
   240	func (e *parallelExecution) startRunner(s *gauge.SpecCollection, stream int) (runner.Runner, []error) {
   241	        if os.Getenv("GAUGE_CUSTOM_BUILD_PATH") == "" {
   242	                _ = os.Setenv("GAUGE_CUSTOM_BUILD_PATH", path.Join(os.Getenv("GAUGE_PROJECT_ROOT"), "gauge_bin"))
   243	        }
   244	        runner, err := runner.Start(e.manifest, stream, make(chan bool), false)
   245	        if err != nil {
   246	                logger.Errorf(true, "Failed to start runner. %s", err.Error())
   247	                logger.Debugf(true, "Skipping %d specifications", s.Size())
   248	                if isLazy() {
   249	                        return nil, []error{fmt.Errorf("Failed to start runner. %s", err.Error())}
   250	                }
   251	                return nil, []error{streamExecError{specsSkipped: s.SpecNames(), message: fmt.Sprintf("Failed to start runner. %s", err.Error())}}
   252	        }
   253	        return runner, nil
   254	}
   255	
   256	func (e *parallelExecution) startSpecsExecutionWithRunner(s *gauge.SpecCollection, runner runner.Runner, stream int) {
   257	        executionInfo := newExecutionInfo(s, runner, e.pluginHandler, e.errMaps, false, stream)
   258	        se := newSimpleExecution(executionInfo, false, false)
   259	        se.execute()
   260	        err := runner.Kill()
   261	        if err != nil {
   262	                logger.Errorf(true, "Failed to kill runner. %s", err.Error())
   263	        }
   264	        e.resultChan <- se.suiteResult
   265	}
   266	
   267	func (e *parallelExecution) executeSpecsInSerial(s *gauge.SpecCollection) *result.SuiteResult {
   268	        runner, err := e.startRunner(s, 1)
   269	        if err != nil {
   270	                return &result.SuiteResult{UnhandledErrors: err}
   271	        }
   272	        executionInfo := newExecutionInfo(s, runner, e.pluginHandler, e.errMaps, false, 1)
   273	        se := newSimpleExecution(executionInfo, false, false)
   274	        se.execute()
   275	        er := runner.Kill()
   276	        if er != nil {
   277	                logger.Errorf(true, "Failed to kill runner. %s", er.Error())
   278	        }
   279	
   280	        return se.suiteResult
   281	}
   282	
   283	func (e *parallelExecution) finish() {
   284	        e.suiteResult = mergeDataTableSpecResults(e.suiteResult)
   285	        event.Notify(event.NewExecutionEvent(event.SuiteEnd, nil, e.suiteResult, 0, &gauge_messages.ExecutionInfo{}))
   286	        message := &gauge_messages.Message{
   287	                MessageType: gauge_messages.Message_SuiteExecutionResult,
   288	                SuiteExecutionResult: &gauge_messages.SuiteExecutionResult{
   289	                        SuiteResult: gauge.ConvertToProtoSuiteResult(e.suiteResult),
   290	                },
   291	        }
   292	        e.pluginHandler.NotifyPlugins(message)
   293	        e.pluginHandler.GracefullyKillPlugins()
   294	}
   295	
   296	func (e *parallelExecution) aggregateResults(suiteResults []*result.SuiteResult) {
   297	        r := result.NewSuiteResult(ExecuteTags, e.startTime)
   298	        if e.suiteResult != nil {
   299	                r.PreHookMessages = e.suiteResult.PreHookMessages
   300	                r.PreHookScreenshotFiles = e.suiteResult.PreHookScreenshotFiles
   301	                r.PostHookMessages = e.suiteResult.PostHookMessages
   302	                r.PostHookScreenshotFiles = e.suiteResult.PostHookScreenshotFiles
   303	        }
   304	        for _, suiteResult := range suiteResults {
   305	                r.SpecsFailedCount += suiteResult.SpecsFailedCount
   306	                r.SpecResults = append(r.SpecResults, suiteResult.SpecResults...)
   307	                r.PreHookMessages = append(r.PreHookMessages, suiteResult.PreHookMessages...)
   308	                r.PreHookScreenshotFiles = append(r.PreHookScreenshotFiles, suiteResult.PreHookScreenshotFiles...)
   309	                r.PostHookMessages = append(r.PostHookMessages, suiteResult.PostHookMessages...)
   310	                r.PostHookScreenshotFiles = append(r.PostHookScreenshotFiles, suiteResult.PostHookScreenshotFiles...)
   311	                if suiteResult.IsFailed {
   312	                        r.IsFailed = true
   313	                }
   314	                if suiteResult.PreSuite != nil {
   315	                        r.PreSuite = suiteResult.PreSuite
   316	                }
   317	                if suiteResult.PostSuite != nil {
   318	                        r.PostSuite = suiteResult.PostSuite
   319	                }
   320	                if suiteResult.UnhandledErrors != nil {
   321	                        r.UnhandledErrors = append(r.UnhandledErrors, suiteResult.UnhandledErrors...)
   322	                }
   323	        }
   324	        r.ExecutionTime = int64(time.Since(e.startTime) / 1e6)
   325	        e.suiteResult = r
   326	        e.suiteResult.SetSpecsSkippedCount()
   327	}
   328	
   329	func isLazy() bool {
   330	        return strings.ToLower(Strategy) == Lazy
   331	}
   332	
   333	func isValidStrategy(strategy string) bool {
   334	        strategy = strings.ToLower(strategy)
   335	        return strategy == Lazy || strategy == Eager
   336	}
   337	
   338	func (e *parallelExecution) isMultithreaded() bool {
   339	        if !env.EnableMultiThreadedExecution() {
   340	                return false
   341	        }
   342	        if !e.runners[0].IsMultithreaded() {
   343	                logger.Warningf(true, "Runner doesn't support mutithreading, using multiprocess parallel execution.")
   344	                return false
   345	        }
   346	        return true
   347	}

2026-05-29 20:04:54,483 - INFO - swea-agent-getgauge__gauge-2836 - 💭 THOUGHT
Both parallel execution paths use `newSimpleExecution` which creates `specExecutor` and calls its `execute` method, which calls `executeScenario`. So my fix applies to all execution paths.

Now I'm thinking about whether there's another issue I missed. Let me re-read the PR description:

> --failed performs retry for passed tests with --max-retry-count flag
> When max-retry-count is enabled and after that a gauge run --failed is performed, specs that passed with --max-retry-count will be executed anyway as if they failed.

So the issue is that specs/scenarios that passed (perhaps after some retries) are still being executed with `--failed`. My fix addresses this by removing scenarios that pass from the failedItemsMap.

But there's another subtlety: the `addSpecFailedMetadata` function deletes all scenario-level entries for a spec and replaces with the spec-level filename. This happens on `SpecEnd` if there are pre/post hook failures. If a spec has no hook failures, this function is not called, and only scenario-level entries are used.

What if a spec has some scenarios that failed and some that passed after retry, and no hook failures? The failed scenarios remain in `failedItemsMap`, and the passed ones are removed (by my fix). When `--failed` runs, only the failed scenarios are re-executed. Correct.

What if a spec has all scenarios passing after retry, and no hook failures? All scenarios are removed from `failedItemsMap`, making it empty for that spec. The spec is not re-executed. Correct.

But there's another edge case: what if a spec has NO scenarios (e.g., only a table with no scenarios)? Then no scenario-level events are fired. The spec would be considered passed (no failures). This is fine.

Now, I'm fairly confident that my fix is correct. However, I also want to check if there's any issue with the `addSpecFailedMetadata` being called even when the spec has no failed scenarios but has hook failures. In that case, the spec-level filename is added, and the spec is re-executed with `--failed`. But if the spec had no scenarios, there would be no scenario-level entries to delete. This is fine.

But what if the spec has hook failures AND some scenarios that passed after retry? The hook failures cause `addSpecFailedMetadata` to delete all scenario-level entries and replace with the spec filename. This means even scenarios that passed after retry would be re-executed. But this is correct because the hook failure is at the spec level, affecting all scenarios.

I think my fix is complete. Let me also double-check the `addFailedMetadata` function signature:

```go
func addFailedMetadata(res result.Result, args []string, add func(res result.Result, args []string)) {
    if len(res.GetPostHook()) > 0 || len(res.GetPreHook()) > 0 {
        add(res, args)
    }
}
```

This function is called on `SpecEnd` and `SuiteEnd`. On `SpecEnd`, it calls `addSpecFailedMetadata`. On `SuiteEnd`, it calls `addSuiteFailedMetadata`.

For `addSpecFailedMetadata`:
- It only runs if spec has pre/post hook failures.
- It deletes all scenario-level entries and adds the spec-level filename.

For `addSuiteFailedMetadata`:
- It only runs if suite has pre/post hook failures.
- It clears the entire map and repopulates with the args (spec dirs).

Both of these are correct for their respective scopes.

Now, I'm thinking about whether there's a potential issue with the order of events. The events are:
1. `ScenarioEnd` - multiple times (once per scenario per retry)
2. `SpecEnd` - once per spec
3. `SuiteEnd` - once per suite

The `ListenFailedScenarios` goroutine processes these events sequentially. So for a given spec:
1. Multiple `ScenarioEnd` events are processed (adding/removing scenarios)
2. `SpecEnd` event is processed (if hook failures, replaces scenario-level with spec-level)
3. After all specs, `SuiteEnd` event is processed (if suite hook failures, clears and uses args; then aggregates and writes)

The order is correct.

Now, one final consideration: what if a scenario fails on the first attempt, passes on the second, but then the SPEC has a post-hook failure? The `SpecEnd` event would call `addSpecFailedMetadata`, which deletes all scenario-level entries and adds the spec-level filename. The scenario that passed after retry would be included (because the whole spec is marked as failed). This is correct because the spec-level hook failure means the spec failed.

Similarly, if the SUITE has a post-hook failure, `addSuiteFailedMetadata` would clear everything and use the args. This is correct.

I believe my fix is complete and correct.

Let me now also check if there's a need to update the test file for the rerun package to include tests for the new behavior (removing scenarios that pass). But the user said: "I've already taken care of all changes to any of the test files described in the <pr_description>." So I don't need to modify test files.
